<section type="Titlepage">
A DICTIONARY 
in Englyshe and Welshe moche ne&#173;
cessary to all suche Welshemen as
wil spedly learne the englyshe t<expan type="">on</expan>gue
thought vnto the kynges maie&#173;
stie very mete to be sette for&#173;
the to the vse of his graces
subiectes in Wales: whe&#173;
revnto is <expan type="">pre</expan>fixed a litle
treaty so of the eng&#173;
glyshe pron<expan type="">un</expan>cia&#173;
cion of the let&#173;
ters, by
Wyllyam Salesbury
</section>

</page>

<page sig="a1v">
<section type="Dedication">
&leaf; TO THE MOOST VIC&#173;
toriouse &#38; Redowbtede prince Henry theyght
by the grace of God Kynge of Englande,
Fraunce and Irelande defender of the
faythe And of the Churche of En&#173;
glande and also of Irel<expan type="">an</expan>de in
erthe the supreame Hedde
be al prosperitye in
continuall
honour

WHere as emongeste other
sondrye &#38; manifolde good
and godlye ordinaunces
bothe mooste wyselye inu<expan type="">en</expan><emend err="">&#173;</emend>
tede &#38; mooste effectuously
performede and put in vse
by your grace moste noble
and Redoubtede Prynce,
Wherby youre Royalmes and dominions ha&#173;
ue receaued infinitte c<expan type="">om</expan>modyties and auoyded
greate displeasures and disturbaunce whyche
bothe nowe disquiet other Royalmes and befo<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
re your graces tyme hath also vexed thys your
Royalme of Englande: your excell<expan type="">en</expan>t wysdome
(as you haue an eye to euery parte and membre
of your Dominion) hath causede to be enactede
and stably shede by your moste cheffe &#38; heghest
counsayl of the parlyament, that there shal her&#173;
after be no differ<expan type="">en</expan>ce in lawes and language by&#173;
twyxte youre subiectes of youre principalytye

</page>

<page sig="a2r">
of Wales and your other subiectes of your Ro<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
yalme of Englande mooste prudently consyde&#173;
rynge what great hatred debate &#38; scryffe hathe
rysen emongeste men by reason of dyuersitie of
language and what a bonde and knotte of lo&#173;
ue and frendshyppe the c<expan type="">om</expan>munion of one tonge
is, &#38; that also by the iudgement of all wyse men
it is moost conueniente and mete that they that
be vnder domini<expan type="">on</expan> of one most gracious Hedde
and Kynge shal vse also one l<expan type="">an</expan>guage and that
euen as theyr hertes agree in loue and obedi<expan type="">en</expan>ce
to your grace so may also theyr tongues agree
in one kynd of speche &#38; language: Therfore I
vnderstandynge that it is the dutye of all your
graces louynge subiectes not onely th<expan type="">em</expan> selfe to
obey your graces wyl and pleasure but also as
moch as lyeth in them, bothe to encourage and
further al other to the same Where as many o&#173;
ther of excellent witte and learnynge haue done
greate seruice to your grace in great &#38; weightie
maters I also emongeste the reste, accordynge
to my small talent, thought it my duty to att<expan type="">em</expan>p<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
te alwayes I coulde to brynge, although smal
although lytle, yet some helpe at the leaste wyse
towarde the accomplyshement of youre mooste
gracyouse pleasure Wherfore seyng ther is ma<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ny of your graces subiectes in Wales that rea<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
dethe parfytlye, the welshe tonge whych if they
had, englyshe expounded in the welshe speche,
myght be bothe theyr owne scholemaysters and
other mennes also, and therby most spedely ob&#173;
teyne the knolege of the englishe t<expan type="">on</expan>ge through

For as S
Paul sa&#173;
yeth if I
knowe
not what
the lang&#173;
uage me&#173;
aneth, I
shalbe vn
to hym <expan type="">that</expan>
speaketh
an alient
&#38; he that
speaketh
shalbe an
alient vn
to me. i.
Cor.xiiii

</page>

<page sig="a2v">
owt all the countraye I haue writt<expan type="">en</expan> a lytle en&#173;
glyshe dyctionary with the welshe interpreta&#173;
cion wher vnto I haue prefixed a treatyse of the
englyshe pronunciation of the letters: and al&#173;
though that nother the boke it selfe entreating
of a matter byfore towchede of no man &#38; ther&#173;
fore rude (as all thynges be at their furst bygin<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
nynge) can be in no poynte worthye to be offere<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
de to your maiestie And I agayne of such sym&#173;
ple both witte and learnyng and of such a mea&#173;
ne &#38; lowe estate that I am most vnworthe to de<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
dicate any thynge vnto your grace althoughe
of it selfe it were veraye excellent, yet the cons&#173;
cience of my most feruent loue towarde youre
grace and most vehement desyre to accomplishe
your wyll to my power hathe made me bolde e&#173;
mongeste other large and greate gyuers after
thex<expan type="">am</expan>ple of the poore widdowe (whom the Gos&#173;
pel speaketh of) to offer vp to youre grace
my lytle farthyng as a testimonye
of mi due bonden loue towardes
youre maiestie whom Ihesu
the eternal Kynge preser<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ue longe in al prospe&#173;
ritye &#38; most highe
honoure.

Youre poore and humble subiecte
Wyllyam Salesburye.

<note type="m">
Luc.xxi.</note>
</section>

</page>

<heading>
&#182; Natur a sain y llythyreu
vchod yn Saesnec.
</heading>

A Seisnic sydd vn natur ac (a)
gymreic / val y may yn eg&#173;
lur yn y gertieu hyn o saes&#173;
nec ale/ aal: ac ymhymraec
kwrw: pale paal: lale sal:
O ddieithyr Ry w amser y
kaifs/a/ sam y dipton (aw)
yn en wedic pan ddel ef o vl&#173;
ayn l/ne ll/val y may yn egsurach dr wy y geirieu
hynn:</term> <term lang="en">balde</term> <term lang="we">bawld moel</term> <term lang="en">ball</term>, <term lang="we">bawl pel:</term> <term lang="en">wall</term> <term lang="we">wa&#173;

<page sig="s3v">
<term lang="we">
&#182; Iohan Waley y prenter yn danfon
anerch ar popol Kymry.))

WElwch karedigon Gymry mi ddoetha ac a
prentais hydic nifer o ry w lyfreu hyn w th
ddeissyf gwr banhedic och gwlad yr hwn
a dystolaythei i mi y kaffwn chwi yn morh
rhwyddon vargenwyr mor hynaws gyfeddachwyr
ac morh vonheddigaidd awch kyueillach ac y bythei
dredifarus ym a gymereis o boen a thrauael a chost yn
awch pleit: yr hyn o phrofwch yn gyfagos i wir, gwy&#173;
byddwch y kymeraf amser arall angwanec o lafur
mewn suwt petheu or eino wch er awch mwyn: Eithyr
yn awr ni chefeis o enhyd printo pop gair kyn ddifeied
na chyn gywired ac y mynysswn Herwydd paam od
gwelaf y gallwyf vod ynkyfemyl digolled o ymarfer
o brinto ywch: ef vydd diueiach a dieskeulussach
pop rhan om gorchwyl y waith nessaf a
dew or blayn yr hwn ach kattwo ar
i lwybyr ef yn wastadawl.
poet gwir.</term>

&#182; Imprynted at London in
Foster lane, by me
Ioh&#241; waley.))

(1547.)

<term lang="la">Cum priuilegio ad imprimendum solum.</term>

</page>
</leme>
